Source pages p. 297

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the philosophers' claim that the soul can return to its exact earthly body. Ghazali classifies this as the second division (the first being the denial of bodily resurrection altogether). He first states that even if conceivable, the return would be a resumption of the soul's administration of the body, but it is impossible because the body decomposes and its matter disperses into the environment. Even if we appeal to God's power, there are two options: gathering only the parts at death—which would lead to absurd and unseemly resurrections of amputees and the emaciated, especially in Paradise—or gathering all parts the person ever had, which is impossible for two reasons: first, due to cannibalism, where one body's matter becomes another's, making it impossible to assign the same particles to two souls; second, due to inter-organ nourishment within a single body, where a part like the liver may have been composed partly of material that was once part of the heart, so to which organ should that particle be returned? Ghazali then strengthens the argument by noting that even without cannibalism, normal biological cycles of growth, decay, and consumption mean that every particle of earth has been part of countless human bodies, making it impossible to allocate finite matter to infinite souls (a third impossibility). Thus, the return of the soul to its identical body is impossible in multiple ways.

Key Terms
غذاء (nourishment)
أجزاء عضوية (organic parts)
كبد (liver)
قلب (heart)
تربة (soil)
نبات (plants)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That God can simply create new matter for each body.
Correction: Ghazali's argument assumes the philosophers' claim that it is the same physical matter. He shows the absurdities that follow from that assumption.

Checkpoint
According to Ghazali, why does inter-organ nourishment make resurrection of the same body impossible?
A) Organs are too complex to replicate
B) The same particle may have been part of multiple organs, so it is unclear where to assign it
C) Medical science proves organs cannot function after death
D) The soul cannot inhabit a body with multiple organ parts

Key Takeaway
The problem of shared matter, both between bodies and within a single body, makes the philosophers' theory of bodily resurrection logically impossible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever assumed that your body is uniquely yours, made of 'your' material? This lesson shows every particle of your body was once part of someone else. How does that humbling truth change your sense of ownership and identity before the Creator? What will you do this week to remind yourself that you are not an independent being but a loan of matter from the earth?
?
If resurrection is not about reassembling the same stuff, then what makes you 'you' in the afterlife? The philosophers' mechanical view failed because it limited God's power. Where in your life have you reduced God's ability to act—perhaps by relying on your own plans, resources, or understanding? Commit one area of your life today where you will consciously trust God's absolute power to do what seems impossible to you.

The Infinity of Souls and Finitude of Matter
Ghazali presents a third impossibility: infinite souls cannot be accommodated by finite matter.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Ghazali's third impossibility: the number of human souls is infinite, but the amount of physical matter is finite, so there cannot be enough matter for all bodies.

Core Idea
Infinite souls cannot be paired with finite matter.

Ghazali concludes his refutation with a powerful metaphysical argument: if human souls are infinite and have been existing through endless cycles of life and death, and physical matter is finite, then there simply is not enough material to provide bodies for all souls. This contradiction shows that the philosophers' theory is impossible.

Guided Path
1
Read the final Arabic passage
Focus on the phrase 'النفوس المفارقة للأبدان غير متناهية، والأبدان أجسام متناهية'.
2
Understand the premise
Ghazali assumes that souls are created with each person and survive death. Over countless generations, the number of souls is potentially infinite.
He does not argue for this premise here but uses it.
3
See the contradiction
Physical matter (bodies) is finite and limited. If there are infinite souls, they cannot all be provided with bodies composed of finite matter.
This is a quantitative argument.
4
Reflect on the implication
This shows that even if the material could be reassigned, there would not be enough particles to go around for all souls.
Ghazali concludes that the material 'falls short' of the souls.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما القسم الثاني، وهو تقدير بقاء النفس وردها إلى ذلك البدن بعينه، فهو لو تصور، لكان معاداً، أي عوداً إلى تدبير البدن بعد مفارقته، لكنه محال، إذ بدن الميت يستحيل تراباً، أو تأكله الذيدان والطيور، ويستحيل دماء وبخاراً وهواء، ويمتزج بهواء العالم، وبخاره، ومائه، امتزاجاً يبعد انتزاعه، واستخلاصه. ولكن إن فرض ذلك اتكالا على قدرة الله تعالى، فلا يخلو، إما أن يجمع الأجزاء التي مات عليها فقط، فينبغي أن يعاد الأقطع، ومجذوع والأذن، وناقص الأعضاء، كما كان، وهذا مستقبح لا سيما في أهل الجنة، الأنف وهم الذين خلقوا ناقصين، في ابتداء الفطرة، فإعادتهم إلى ما كانوا عليه، من الهزال عند الموت في غاية النكال هذا إن اقتصر على جمع الأجزاء الموجودة عند الموت وإن جمع جميع أجزائه التي كانت موجودة في جميع عمره، فهو محال من وجهين: أحدهما: أن الإنسان إذا تغذى بلحم إنسان، وقد جرت العادة به في بعض البلاد، ويكثر وقوعه في أوقات القحط. فيتعذر حشرهما جميعاً، لأن مادة واحدة كانت بدناً للمأكول، وصارت بالغذاء بدناً للأكل ولا يمكن رد نفسين إلى بدن واحد. والثاني: أنه يجب أن يعاد جزء واحد، كبداً وقلباً، ويداً، ورجلا، فإنه ثبت بالصناعة الطبية، أن الأجزاء العضوية، يتغذى بعضها، بفضلة غذاء البعض، فيتغذى الكبد بأجزاء القلب، وكذلك سائر الأعضاء، فنفرض أجزاء معينة، قد كانت مادة الجملة من الأعضاء، فإلى أي عضو تعاد؟!! بل لا يحتاج في تقرير الاستحالة الأولى إلى أكل الناس الناس فإنك إذا تأملت ظاهر التربة المعمورة، علمت بعد طول الزمان، أن ترابها جثث الموتى، قد تتربت وزرع فيها وغرس، وصارت حبا وفاكهة، وتناولتها الدواب، فصارت لحماً، وتناولناها فصارت أبداناً لنا، فما من مادة يشار إليها، إلا وقد كانت بدناً لأناس كثيرين، فاستحالت وصارت تراباً، ثم نباتاً ثم لحماً، ثم حيواناً. بل يلزم منه محال ثالث، وهو أن النفوس المفارقة للأبدان، غير متناهية، والأبدان أجسام متناهية، فلا تفى المواد، التي كانت مواد الإنسان، بأنفس الناس كلهم، بل تضيق عنهم.
As for the second division, which is the supposition of the soul's survival and its return to that identical body—if it were conceivable, it would be a return (ma‘ād), i.e., a return to administering the body after separation, but it is impossible. For the dead body turns into dust, or is eaten by worms and birds, and turns into blood, vapor, and air, and mixes with the air of the world, its vapor, and its water, in a mixture that makes its extraction and recovery unlikely. But if that is supposed relying on the power of Allah the Exalted, then it is either that He gathers only the parts present at death, so the amputee, the one with a cut ear, and the one with missing limbs should be returned as they were, and this is repugnant, especially in the case of the people of Paradise—the nose?—[and those who were created deficient from the beginning of their natural constitution; returning them to what they were, of emaciation at death, is an extreme punishment]. This is if He restricts Himself to gathering the parts present at death. And if He gathers all his parts that existed throughout his entire life, it is impossible in two ways. One of them: that if a human feeds on the flesh of a human—as is customary in some lands and occurs frequently in times of famine—then the resurrection of both becomes impossible, because one matter was the body of the eaten and became through nutrition the body of the eater, and it is impossible to return two souls to one body. And the second: that a single part—like liver, heart, hand, foot—must be returned, for it is established by medical science that organic parts are nourished by the surplus food of other parts, so the liver is nourished by parts of the heart, and likewise the rest of the organs. So if we suppose specific parts that were the material of the whole aggregate of organs, to which organ should they be returned?! Rather, one does not even need cannibalism to establish the first impossibility. For if you reflect on the surface of the inhabited earth, you know that after a long time its soil consists of the corpses of the dead, which have become dust, then crops have been sown and planted in it, and become grain and fruit, then animals have eaten them and they become flesh, then we have eaten them and they become our bodies. So there is no material that can be pointed to that has not been the body of many people, so it has transformed and become dust, then plants, then flesh, then animals. Rather, a third impossibility follows from it: that the souls separate from bodies are infinite, while bodies are finite bodies, so the materials that were the materials of humans are insufficient for all the souls of people, nay, they fall short of them.
Source pages p. 297

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the philosophers' claim that the soul can return to its exact earthly body. Ghazali classifies this as the second division (the first being the denial of bodily resurrection altogether). He first states that even if conceivable, the return would be a resumption of the soul's administration of the body, but it is impossible because the body decomposes and its matter disperses into the environment. Ghazali then strengthens the argument by noting that even without cannibalism, normal biological cycles of growth, decay, and consumption mean that every particle of earth has been part of countless human bodies, making it impossible to allocate finite matter to infinite souls (a third impossibility). Thus, the return of the soul to its identical body is impossible in multiple ways.

متناهية (finite)
غير متناهية (infinite)
مواد (materials)

Misconception: That God can create new matter for each soul.
Correction: The philosophers' theory requires the same matter to be reused; creating new matter would be a different kind of resurrection, which they deny.

Ghazali's Two Arguments Against Returning Soul to Any Human Body
Ghazali enumerates two reasons for the impossibility of returning the soul to any human body.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Ghazali's two reasons for the impossibility of the soul returning to any arbitrarily chosen human body.

Core Idea
Finite matter cannot host infinite souls; raw matter cannot be ensouled.

In this passage, Ghazali refutes the idea that the soul can return to a human body made from any material whatsoever. He presents two distinct arguments: one based on the finitude of sublunar matter versus the infinitude of souls, and another on the necessary preparation of matter to receive a soul. This lesson unpacks both reasons and their implications.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation once to grasp Ghazali's overall argument. Note that he lists two reasons, though the second is incomplete in the source.
The passage cuts off mid-sentence; focus on the two reasons as given.
2
Identify the two reasons
Locate the first reason (finite matter vs. infinite souls) and the second reason (dust requires transformation). Understand how each independently proves impossibility.
3
Reflect on Ghazali's method
Consider why Ghazali uses natural-philosophical premises (the concave of the moon, generation/corruption) to argue against a theological claim. This shows his dialectical engagement with Aristotelian cosmology.
This connects to the broader Tahafut project of refuting philosophers on their own terms.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما القسم الثالث، وهو رد النفس إلى بدن إنساني من أى مادة كانت، وأى تراب اتفق، فهو محال من وجهين: أحدهما: أن المواد القابلة للكون والفساد، محصورة في مقعر فلك القمر، لا يمكن عليها مزيد، وهي متناهية، والأنفس المفارقة للأبدان، غير متناهية، فلا تفي بها. والثاني: أن التراب لا يقبل تدبير النفس، ما بقى تراباً، بل لا بد أن تمتزج العناصر امتزاجاً، يضاهى امتزاج النطفة، بل الخشب والحديد، لا يقبل
As for the third division—which is the return of the soul to a human body of whatever matter it might be, and whatever dust it may happen to be—it is impossible in two ways. One: that the materials susceptible to generation and corruption are confined within the concave of the sphere of the moon; no increase is possible upon them, and they are finite, while the souls separate from bodies are infinite, so the materials are insufficient for them. And the second: that dust does not accept the administration of the soul as long as it remains dust; rather, the elements must mix in a mixture resembling the mixture of the sperm. Indeed, wood and iron do not accept...
Source pages p. 298

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of a third possible position: that the soul returns to a brand-new human body made from any matter (not necessarily its original body). Ghazali gives two reasons for its impossibility. First, the material available in the sublunar world (the region of generation and corruption) is finite, whereas the number of human souls that have ever existed is potentially infinite (or at least very large), so there is insufficient matter to provide distinct bodies for all souls. Second, dust (or any raw matter) cannot directly be ensouled; it must undergo a specific mixture similar to the formation of sperm, which requires a particular process. The text cuts off mid-sentence, but the implication is that mere dust or materials like wood and iron cannot receive the soul without proper preparation, and that preparation is not guaranteed for every soul. Thus, the philosophers' hope for any arbitrary matter to serve as the resurrected body is futile.

Key Terms
كون وفساد (generation and corruption)
مقعر فلك القمر (concave of the lunar sphere)
تدبير النفس (administration of the soul)
امتزاج (mixture)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That any matter can become a human body by divine fiat without natural prerequisites.
Correction: Ghazali insists that the soul-body union requires natural prerequisites: the matter must be suitable and prepared (e.g., through proper mixture). Even God's power (in the philosophers' framework) is subject to these natural conditions.

Checkpoint

C) Because the soul must always return to its original body

Key Takeaway
Ghazali refutes the idea of the soul returning to any human body by arguing that finite sublunar matter cannot accommodate infinite souls, and raw matter must undergo specific preparation to receive a soul.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?
Ghazali says dust cannot directly receive the soul; the elements must mix in a specific way. Your body came from such a mixture. Are you treating it as a mere lump of matter, or as a specially prepared vessel for your soul?
?
The soul's return to any body is impossible. Your soul will only be united with a body that God has prepared. Does this thought fill you with awe and accountability for how you live now?

The Philosophers' Second Objection: Gradual Transformation vs. Instant Miracle
Philosophers argue iron-to-cloth change requires gradual elemental stages.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the philosophers argue that turning iron into cloth must occur through gradual elemental stages, not instantaneously.

Core Idea
Instant change is impossible; only gradual transformation through stages is rational.

In this passage, Ghazali presents the philosophers' argument that no power can directly turn iron into woven cloth. They insist that any such transformation must follow a natural sequence of decomposition and recombination through elemental stages. This objection is aimed at miraculous bodily resurrection, which would seem to bypass such gradual processes. However, the philosophers concede that these stages could occur so rapidly as to appear instantaneous.

Guided Path
1
Read the philosophers' claim
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Notice how the philosophers state their main claim: iron cannot be turned directly into cloth.
They use the phrase 'ليس فى المقدور' (it is not within capability).
2
Identify the required stages
The passage lists a sequence of transformations: decomposition into elements, recombination into cotton, then yarn, then weaving. Make a mental note of each stage.
The stages are: simple elements → cotton → yarn → woven cloth.
3
Consider the philosophers' concession
Notice that they allow for rapid succession: if the stages happen quickly, one might think it occurred at once. This is important for the debate on miracles.
4
Reflect on the underlying assumption
Ask yourself: what principle of causality does this objection rely on? The philosophers assume that change must follow natural patterns and cannot skip steps.
This connects to Ghazali's larger critique of necessary causation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المسلك الثانى أن قالوا : ليس فى المقدور ، أن يقلب الحديد ثوباً منسوجاً بحيث تنعم به الأجسام ، إلا بأن تتحلل أجزاء الحديد ، إلى بسائط العناصر ، بأسباب تستولى على الحديد ، فتحلله إلى بسائط العناصر ، ثم تجتمع العناصر ، وتدار في أطوار في الخلقة، إلى أن تكتسب صورة القطن ، ثم يكتسب القطن ، صورة الغزل ، ثم الغزل يكتسب الانتظام المعلوم ، الذي هو النسج ، على هيأة معلومة ، ولو قيل : إن قلب الحديد ، عمامة قطنية، ممكن من غير الاستحالة في هذه الأطوار ، على سبيل الترتيب ، لكان محالا نعم يجوز أن يخطر ببال الإنسان ، أن هذه الاستحالات يجوز أن تحصل كلها في زمان متقارب ، لا يحس الإنسان بطوله ، فيظن أنه وقع ، فجأة دفعة واحدة
The second way: they said: It is not within capability that iron be turned into a woven garment such that bodies are benefited by it, except by the decomposition of the parts of iron into the simple elements, by means that take hold of the iron and decompose it into the simple elements. Then the elements come together and are turned through stages in creation until they acquire the form of cotton. Then cotton acquires the form of yarn. Then yarn acquires the known ordering which is weaving, in a known shape. And if it were said that the turning of iron into a cotton turban is possible without going through these stages in order, it would be impossible. Yes, it may occur to a person's mind that these transformations could all happen in a short period, whose length he does not perceive, so he thinks that it occurred suddenly all at once.
Source pages p. 300

Commentary
This passage presents the philosophers' second objection against bodily resurrection. They argue that it is impossible to directly transform iron into a woven garment for the body's benefit. The only way is a gradual process: iron must first be decomposed into its elemental components, then those elements must recombine through various stages to become cotton, then yarn, then woven fabric. Claiming that iron could become cloth instantly without these stages is absurd. However, the philosophers concede that one might imagine these transformations happening so quickly that they appear instantaneous. This sets up the problem for resurrection: if the resurrection body must be reconstituted from earth, it would require a similarly gradual process, not an instantaneous miracle.

Key Terms
بسائط العناصر
الاستحالة
أطوار

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The philosophers completely deny any transformation of iron to cloth.
Correction: They allow transformation through gradual stages; they only deny instantaneous, stage-skipping change.

Checkpoint
According to the philosophers, what is the only way to turn iron into woven cloth?
A) Through a direct miracle
B) Through gradual decomposition and recombination of elements
C) Through alchemy
D) Through divine command 'Be'

Key Takeaway
The philosophers argue that any transformation must follow natural stages; instantaneous change violates causal order, though rapid succession is acceptable.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a long, difficult process in your life, do you trust that God could suddenly resolve it if He wills, or do you assume it must unfold stage by stage? How does this lesson challenge the way you wait for His help?
?
Have you ever secretly doubted a miracle—whether in the Quran or in your own life—because it seemed to violate the natural order you observe every day? What would it mean for your faith to truly accept that God is not bound by causality?
?
Imagine standing before Allah on the Day of Judgment, your body recreated not through natural stages but by His direct command. Does that thought comfort you or unsettle you? Why—and what does your reaction reveal about your reliance on nature versus your reliance on the Creator?

The Philosophers' Argument: Gradual Necessity of Resurrection
Ghazali presents the philosophers' argument that resurrection requires gradual transformation in matter.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the philosophers' argument that bodily resurrection cannot occur instantaneously but requires a gradual sequence of material transformations.

Core Idea
Resurrection without gradual stages is as impossible as iron turning into a turban instantaneously.

Before refuting the philosophers, Ghazali presents their strongest objection: that resurrection requires a long causal chain from dust to human. This lesson examines that argument in detail, using the vivid analogy of iron becoming cotton cloth.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the analogy
Read the first part where Ghazali describes the transformation of iron into a cotton turban through stages. Notice the emphasis on order and impossibility without stages.
2
Trace the chain of human composition
Follow the subsequent breakdown of the human body: from food to humors, to bones and flesh, to limbs. See how each step depends on previous ones.
The argument claims this chain is necessary.
3
Understand the conclusion
The passage concludes that saying 'Be' to dust is unintelligible because dust cannot be addressed, and transformation without stages is impossible. Therefore, resurrection is impossible according to the philosophers.
Remember: this is Ghazali's presentation of the opposing view.
4
Distinguish Ghazali's position from the argument
The common misunderstanding is that this is Ghazali's own belief. It is not; he is setting up an objection he will refute later.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بأسباب تستولى على الحديد ، فتحلله إلى بسائط العناصر ، ثم تجتمع العناصر ، وتدار في أطوار في الخلقة، إلى أن تكتسب صورة القطن ، ثم يكتسب القطن صورة الغزل ، ثم الغزل يكتسب الانتظام المعلوم ، الذي هو النسج ، على هيأة معلومة ، ولو قيل : إن قلب الحديد عمامة قطنية ممكن من غير الاستحالة في هذه الأطوار على سبيل الترتيب لكان محالا. نعم يجوز أن يخطر ببال الإنسان أن هذه الاستحالات يجوز أن تحصل كلها في زمان متقارب لا يحس الإنسان بطوله فيظن أنه وقع فجأة دفعة واحدة. وإذا عقل هذا فالإنسان المبعوث المحشور لو كان بدنه من حجر أو ياقوت أو در أو تراب محض لم يكن إنساناً بل لا يتصور أن يكون إنساناً إلا أن يكون متشكلاً بالشكل المخصوص مركباً من العظام والعروق واللحوم والغضاريف والأخلاط. والأجزاء المفردة تتقدم على المركبة فلا يكون البدن ما لم تكن الأعضاء ولا تكون الأعضاء المركبة ما لم تكن العظام واللحوم والعروق ولا تكون هذه المفردات ما لم تكن الأخلاط ولا تكون الأخلاط الأربعة ما لم تكن موادها من الغذاء ولا يكون الغذاء ما لم يكن حيوان أو نبات وهو اللحم والحبوب ولا يكون حيوان ونبات ما لم تكن العناصر الأربعة جميعاً ممتزجة بشرائط مخصوصة طويلة أكثر مما فصلنا جملتها. فإذن لا يمكن أن يتجدد بدن إنسان لترد النفس إليه إلا بهذه الأمور ولها أسباب كثيرة. أفينقلب التراب إنساناً بأن يقال له كن ؟ أو بأن تمهد أسباب انقلابه في هذه الأدوار ؟! وأسبابه هي إلقاء النطفة المستخرجة من لباب بدن الإنسان في رحم حتى يستمد من دم الطمث ومن الغذاء مدة طويلة حتى يتخلق مضغة ثم علقة ثم جنيناً ثم طفلاً ثم شباباً ثم كهلاً ثم شيخاً. فقول القائل يقال له كن فيكون غير معقول إذ التراب لا يخاطب وانقلابه إنساناً دون تردده في هذه الأطوار محال وتردده في هذه الأطوار دون جريان هذه الأسباب محال فيكون البعث محالا.
By causes that take hold of iron, breaking it down into the simple elements, then the elements come together and are turned through stages in creation until they acquire the form of cotton, then the cotton acquires the form of yarn, then the yarn acquires the known order which is weaving, in a known manner. And if it were said that the transformation of iron into a cotton turban is possible without undergoing these stages in order, it would be impossible. Yes, it is possible that it occurs to one's mind that these transformations could all occur in a close period of time, of which one does not perceive the length, so one thinks it happened suddenly all at once. And if this is understood, then the resurrected human being, if his body were of stone or ruby or pearl or pure dust, would not be a human; rather, it is not conceivable that he be a human unless he is formed in the specific shape, composed of bones, veins, flesh, cartilage, and humors. And the simple parts precede the composite: the body does not exist without the limbs, the composite limbs do not exist without the bones, flesh, and veins, these simple parts do not exist without the humors, the four humors do not exist without their materials from food, food does not exist without an animal or plant—which is meat and grains—and an animal or plant does not exist unless all four elements are mixed under specific and lengthy conditions, more than we have summarized. Therefore, it is not possible for a human body to be renewed for the soul to return to it except through these matters, and they have many causes. So does dust turn into a human by saying to it 'Be'? Or by preparing the causes of its transformation in these stages? Its causes are the casting of the extracted sperm from the core of the human body into a womb, until it draws from menstrual blood and from food for a long period until it becomes a clot, then a clinging form, then an embryo, then an infant, then a youth, then an adult, then an elder. So the saying of one who says 'Be' and it is, is unintelligible, for dust is not addressed, and its transformation into a human without passing through these stages is impossible, and its passing through these stages without the occurrence of these causes is impossible, so resurrection is impossible.
Source pages p. 301

Commentary
This passage presents the philosophers' argument that bodily resurrection is impossible without undergoing a gradual process of transformation, using the analogy of iron turning into a cotton turban. Ghazali explains that just as iron must first be broken down into elements, then form cotton, then yarn, then woven cloth, so too the human body requires a sequence of stages: from food to animal or plant, to the four humors, to bones, flesh, etc. Without this ordered progression, resurrection would be impossible. Therefore, saying 'Be' to dust is unintelligible because dust cannot be addressed, and changing into a human without these stages is impossible. Thus, the philosophers conclude resurrection is impossible. Ghazali is here presenting the objection that he will later refute.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: This passage represents Ghazali's own view that resurrection is impossible.
Correction: Ghazali is presenting the philosophers' argument in order to refute it later. The passage is part of a dialectical structure.

Checkpoint
According to the argument presented, why is resurrection without gradual stages considered impossible?
A) Because God cannot create a body from dust directly.
B) Because the human body requires a specific composition from prior materials in a fixed order.
C) Because the soul cannot return to a body that was dust.
D) Because the Quran denies it.

Key Takeaway
The philosophers argue that just as a cotton turban cannot arise from iron without gradual stages, the human body cannot be resurrected instantaneously from dust.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite 'Indeed, we belong to Allah, and indeed to Him we will return,' do you ever feel a secret unease that the resurrection might be 'impossible' as the philosophers argue? What does that feeling reveal about your trust in God's absolute power over creation?
?
You rely on causes every day—food to live, sleep to recover. In what areas of your life do you behave as if God cannot act without these causes? How would your life change if you truly believed He could create a human from dust in an instant?
?
The philosophers say the body must go through stages; they cannot conceive of an immediate resurrection. Are there beliefs or habits you hold that you unconsciously deem 'impossible' for God to change in you instantly? Will you sincerely ask Him to break that pattern, trusting His power over your own logic?

Two Possibilities for Resurrection
Ghazali offers two possibilities for resurrection's occurrence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Ghazali presents two equally possible explanations for how resurrection occurs, both grounded in divine power.

Core Idea
Resurrection is possible either by direct divine power or by unknown causes.

Ghazali responds to the objection that resurrection requires gradual stages by affirming that both direct divine intervention and operation through unfamiliar causes are possible. He draws on his earlier arguments about causal habits and the treasury of divine power.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyze it. Then read the translation. Let Ghazali's argument flow.
Notice that he concedes the necessity of stages but questions their mechanism.
2
Identify the two possibilities
The passage presents two ways resurrection could occur. Find where each is introduced and how Ghazali justifies them.
One is direct, the other involves hidden causes.
3
Connect to broader causality discussion
Reflect on how this passage uses the breaking of habits (kharaq al-'adat) and the notion of unknown causes to defend resurrection.
This builds on previous lessons on causality.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الاعتراض ، أنا نسلم أن الترقى فى هذه الأطوار ، لا بد منه ، حتى يصير بدن إنسان، كما لا بد منه حتى يصير الحديد عمامة ، فإنه لو بقى حديداً لما كان ثوباً ، بل لابد أن يصير قطناً ، مغزولا ، ثم منسوجاً ، ولكن ذلك في لحظة ، أو فى مدة ، ممكن ، ولم يبين لنا أن البعث يكون فى أدنى ما يقدر ، إذ يمكن أن يكون جمع العظام ، وإنشاز اللحم ، وإنباته ، في زمان طويل. وليس المناقشة فيه. وإنما النظر فى أن الترقى فى هذه الأطوار ، يحصل بمجرد القدرة ، من غير واسطة ، أو بسبب من الأسباب ، وكلاهما ممكنان عندنا ، على ما ذكرناه في المسألة الأولى من الطبيعيات عند الكلام على إجراء العادات ، وأن المقترنات في الوجود اقترانها ليس على طريق التلازم ، بل العادات يجوز خرقها ، فتحصل بقدرة الله تعالى هذه الأمور ، دون وجود أسبابها. وأما الثانى ، فهو أن نقول : ذلك يكون بأسباب ، ولكن ليس من شرطه ، أن يكون السبب ، هو هذا المعهود ، بل في خزانة المقدورات ، عجائب وغرائب ، لم يطلع عليها ، ينكرها من يظن ، أن لا وجود إلا لما شاهده ، كما ينكر طائفة ، السحر ، والنارنجات ، والطلسمات ، والمعجزات ، والكرامات ثابتة بالاتفاق بأسباب غريبة لا يطلع عليها.
The objection: We concede that progression through these stages is necessary for a human body to come to be, just as it is necessary for iron to become a turban; for if it remained iron it would not be a garment, but it must become cotton, spun, then woven. But that in a moment or in a period of time is possible, and he has not shown us that resurrection is at the shortest possible time, for it is possible that the gathering of bones, raising of flesh, and its growth occur over a long time. The discussion is not about that. Rather, the inquiry is about whether progression through these stages occurs by mere power without any intermediary, or by means of some causes; and both are possible in our view, as we mentioned in the first issue of the natural sciences when discussing the breaking of habits, and that concomitant things in existence are not necessarily connected, but habits can be broken, so these matters come to be by the power of God without the existence of their causes. As for the second, it is that we say: that occurs by causes, but it is not a condition that the cause be this familiar one; rather, in the treasury of things within God's power are wonders and marvels that have not been disclosed, which are denied by one who thinks that nothing exists except what he has witnessed, just as a group denies sorcery, prestidigitation, talismans, miracles, and marvels—which are established by consensus—due to strange causes that are not disclosed.
Source pages p. 302

Commentary
This passage is Ghazali's response to the philosophers' objection. The objector concedes that gradual stages are necessary but argues they could happen in a moment or over a long time, so the debate is not about time but about whether these stages occur by direct divine power or through causes. Ghazali asserts both are possible. First, according to the principle of breaking habits (kharaq al-'adat), God can produce these effects directly without their usual causes. Second, even if through causes, those causes need not be the familiar ones; God's power contains wonders unknown to humans, just as many deny the reality of sorcery, talismans, miracles, and marvels because they have not witnessed their causes. Thus, resurrection is not impossible.

قدرة الله
أسباب غريبة
مقدورات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Ghazali denies all secondary causes in resurrection.
Correction: He actually allows both possibilities: direct creation and operation through hidden, unfamiliar causes.

C) Either by natural causes or by angelic intervention.
D) Either by reincarnation or by spiritual resurrection.

Key Takeaway
Ghazali argues that resurrection is not impossible, as it can occur either by God's direct act or through causes we do not know.

Resurrection's Possibility: Stages and Duration
Ghazali presents and refutes the opponent's impossibility argument.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Ghazali's refutation of the argument that resurrection is impossible because it requires stages that seem impossible without their usual causes.

Core Idea
Stages are necessary but duration is flexible; resurrection can be gradual.

Ghazali begins by presenting the philosophers' objection: dust cannot be addressed, and transformation without stages is impossible, so resurrection is impossible. He then concedes that stages are necessary but argues that they could occur over a long period, not necessarily in an instant. Thus the impossibility claim is not proven.

Guided Path
1
Read the opponent's argument
Read carefully the first part from 'فقول القائل...' to 'فيكون البعث محالا.' Understand the three impossibilities claimed.
2
Analyze Ghazali's response
Ghazali concedes the need for stages but questions the required duration. He uses the analogy of iron becoming a turban.
3
Identify the key point
The opponent has not proven that resurrection must be instantaneous; it could be gradual, so the impossibility is not established.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فقول القائل : يقال له : كن، فيكون غير معقول، إذ التراب لا يخاطب، وانقلابه إنساناً، دون تردده في هذه الأطوار، محال، وتردده في هذه الأطوار، دون جريان هذه الأسباب، محال، فيكون البعث محالا. الاعتراض، أنا نسلم أن الترقى فى هذه الأطوار، لا بد منه، حتى يصير بدن إنسان، كما لا بد منه حتى يصير الحديد عمامة، فإنه لو بقى حديداً لما كان ثوباً، بل لابد أن يصير قطناً، مغزولا، ثم منسوجاً، ولكن ذلك في لحظة، أو فى مدة، ممكن، ولم يبين لنا أن البعث يكون فى أدنى ما يقدر، إذ يمكن أن يكون جمع العظام، وإنشاز اللحم، وإنباته، في زمان طويل. وليس المناقشة فيه. وإنما النظر فى أن الترقى فى هذه الأطوار، يحصل بمجرد القدرة، من غير واسطة، أو بسبب من الأسباب، وكلاهما ممكنان عندنا، على ما ذكرناه في، من الطبيعيات عند الكلام على إجراء العادات، وأن المقترنات في الوجود، اقترانها ليس على طريق التلازم، بل العادات يجوز خرقها، فتحصل بقدرة الله تعالى هذه الأمور، دون وجود أسبابها. وأما الثانى، فهو أن نقول: ذلك يكون بأسباب، ولكن ليس من شرطه، أن يكون السبب، هو هذا المعهود، بل في خزانة المقدورات، عجائب وغرائب، لم يطلع عليها، ينكرها من يظن، أن لا وجود إلا لما شاهده، كما ينكر طائفة، السحر، والنارنجات، والطلسمات، والمعجزات، والكرامات ثابتة - بالاتفاق - بأسباب غريبة، لا يطلع عليها. بل لو لم ير إنسان المغناطيس، وجذ به للحديد، وحكى له ذلك، لاستنكره، وقال: لا يتصور جذب الحديد، إلا بخيط يشد عليه، ويجذب، فإنه المشاهد فى الجذب؛ حتى إذا شاهده تعجب منه، وعلم أن علمه قاصر، عن الإحاطة بعجائب القدرة. وكذلك الملاحدة المنكرون للبعث والنشور، إذا بعثوا من القبور، ورأوا عجائب صنع الله تعالى فيهم، ندموا ندامة لا تنفعهم، ويتحسرون على جحودهم، تحسراً لا يغنيهم، ويقال لهم: « هذا الذي كنتم به تكذبون » كالذي يكذب بالخواص والأشياء الغريبة. بل لو خلق إنسان عاقلا ابتداء، وقيل له: إن هذه النطفة القذرة، المتشابهة الأجزاء، تنقسم أجزاؤها المتشابهة، في رحم آدمية، إلى أعضاء مختلفة، لحمية، وعصبية، وعظمية، وعرقية، وغضروفية، وشحمية، فيكون منها العين، على سبع طبقات مختلفة فى المزاج؛ واللسان، والأسنان، على تفاوتهما في الرخاوة والصلابة، مع تجاورهما، وهلم جرا، إلى البدائع التي في الفطرة - لكان إنكاره أشد من إنكار الملاحدة، حيث قالوا: « كنا عظاماً نخرة . . . الآية ». فليس يتفكر المنكر للبعث، أنه من أين عرف انحصار أسباب الوجود، شاهده، ولم يبعد أن يكون فى إحياء الأبدان، منهاج غير ما شاهده، وقد ورد فى بعض الأخبار: أنه يغمر الأرض فى وقت البعث، مطر، قطراته تشبه النطف، وتختلط بالتراب، فأى بعد فى أن يكون فى الأسباب الإلهية أمر يشبه ذلك، ونحن لا نطلع عليه، ويقتضى ذلك انبعاث الأجساد، واستعدادها لقبول النفوس المحشورة، وهل لهذا الإنكار مستند، إلا الاستبعاد المجرد.
So he who says: 'Be' and it is, is not intelligible, for dust is not addressed, and its transformation into a human without passing through these stages is impossible, and its passing through these stages without the occurrence of these causes is impossible, so the resurrection is impossible. The objection: we concede that progression through these stages is necessary until it becomes a human body, just as it is necessary until iron becomes a turban, for if it remained iron it would not be a garment, but rather it must become cotton, spun, then woven, but that in a moment or in a duration is possible, and he did not make clear to us that the resurrection occurs in the shortest possible time, for it is possible that the gathering of bones, the raising of flesh, and its growth take a long time. And the discussion is not about that. Rather the consideration is that the progression through these stages occurs by mere power without an intermediary, or by a cause from among the causes, and both are possible according to us, as we mentioned in the natural sciences in the discussion of the continuity of habits, and that the conjunctions in existence are not in the way of necessary concomitance, but rather habits may be broken, so these matters occur by the power of God, the Exalted, without the existence of their causes. As for the second, it is that we say: that occurs by causes, but it is not a condition that the cause be this familiar one, but rather in the treasury of possibilities are wonders and marvels that have not been disclosed, which he denies who thinks that nothing exists except what he has witnessed, just as a group denies magic, charms, talismans, miracles, and the extraordinary feats of saints - firmly established by agreement - by strange causes that are not disclosed. Rather, if a man had never seen the magnet and its attraction of iron, and it was related to him, he would reject it and say: the attraction of iron is not conceivable except by a string tied to it and pulled, for that is what is witnessed in attraction, until he sees it and marvels at it and knows that his knowledge is insufficient to encompass the wonders of power. Likewise the atheists who deny the resurrection and the gathering, when they are resurrected from the graves and see the wonders of God's making in them, they will regret a regret that does not benefit them, and they will be remorseful over their denial with a remorse that does not avail them, and it will be said to them: 'This is what you used to deny' like one who denies the properties and strange things. Rather, if an intelligent human were created from the beginning and it was said to him: this filthy drop of fluid, uniform in its parts, its uniform parts divide in a human womb into different members: fleshy, nervous, bony, venous, cartilaginous, and fatty, and from them come the eye of seven different layers in temperament, and the tongue, and the teeth, different in softness and hardness despite their proximity, and so on to the wonders in nature - his denial would be stronger than the denial of the atheists when they said: 'We were decayed bones... [the verse]'. So the denier of resurrection does not reflect: from where does he know the confinement of the causes of existence to what he has witnessed, and it is not remote that in the reviving of bodies there is a method other than what he has witnessed, and it has come in some reports: that at the time of the resurrection, a rain will flood the earth, its drops resembling sperm, and they mix with the dust, so what impossibility is there that in the divine causes there is something resembling that, and we are not informed of it, and that necessitates the rising of the bodies and their readiness to receive the gathered souls, and does this denial have any basis except mere improbability?
Source pages p. 302

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the argument that bodily resurrection is impossible. Ghazali begins by presenting the opponents' objection: to say 'Be' to dust is unintelligible because dust cannot be addressed, and transformation of dust into a human body without passing through natural stages (like conception, growth, etc.) is impossible, and passing through those stages without their usual causes is also impossible, therefore resurrection is impossible. Ghazali's first response is to concede the necessity of stages but to question the required duration. He argues that the stages could occur either in an instant or over a long period—both are possible. The opponent has not specified that resurrection must occur in the shortest time; it could be gradual. Then Ghazali moves to the core of the issue: whether the progression through stages happens by divine power directly without any cause, or through some cause (not necessarily the familiar ones). Both are possible in his view. He references his discussion in natural philosophy where he argued that the constant conjunction of events is not due to necessary causation but to divine habit, which can be broken. So God can bring about these changes directly without their usual causes. The second possibility is that they occur through causes, but not the specific causes we are familiar with. God's treasury of possibilities contains wonders that those who limit existence to what they have witness deny. Ghazali then illustrates with the example of magnetism: someone who has never seen a magnet attract iron would think it impossible without a string, but upon seeing it, he realizes his ignorance. Similarly, atheists who deny resurrection will regret their denial when they witness it. Ghazali then draws a powerful analogy: if a rational person were created from scratch and told about embryological development—from a uniform drop to distinct organs, the eye with seven layers, the tongue and teeth with different textures—his denial would be even stronger than the atheists' denial of resurrection. So the denier of resurrection should reflect: why does he think that the only possible causes are those he has seen? There could be divine methods unknown to him, such as a rain of sperm-like drops at the resurrection. Thus, denial is based on mere improbability, not impossibility.

Key Terms
البعث
الأسباب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Resurrection must be instantaneous to be possible.
Correction: Ghazali shows that stages can occur over a long period, so resurrection does not need to be instantaneous.

Checkpoint
In his first response to the opponent, Ghazali concedes that stages are necessary but argues that:
A) They must occur in a moment.
B) They can occur over a long period.
C) They are not needed at all.
D) They occur by hidden causes.

Key Takeaway
Ghazali refutes the claim of impossibility by showing that resurrection can occur gradually over time, so the opponent's argument fails.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that God can bring back the dead, even if it takes a long time, or do you subconsciously limit His power to instant actions?
?
When you face delays in life, do you become impatient like the opponent who insists on instant transformation, or do you trust that God's timing, whether fast or slow, is perfect?
?
Are you willing to accept that God's ways of working might involve stages and processes, even in matters of resurrection, and still have unwavering faith in His ability to accomplish what seems impossible?

Causality and Created Things
intermediate
5 min
Direct Divine Power or Hidden Causes
Ghazali presents two ways resurrection can occur: directly by divine power or through hidden causes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Ghazali's two possible explanations for how resurrection can occur: either directly by God's power without any cause, or through hidden causes that are unfamiliar to us.

Core Idea
Resurrection is possible either through direct divine action or through hidden causes in God's treasury.

After establishing that stages are necessary but flexible in duration, Ghazali now addresses the deeper question: how do the stages occur? He presents two possibilities—either by God's power alone without any intermediary cause, or by some cause, but not necessarily the ones we know. Both are possible because God can break the habits of nature, and unknown causes exist beyond our experience.

Guided Path
1
Read Ghazali's two possibilities
Read from 'وإنما النظر...' to '...لا يطلع عليها.' Identify the two options: direct power or through causes.
2
Understand the refutation of necessary causation
Ghazali references his earlier discussion about habits: conjunctions in existence are not necessary but based on habit, and God can break them.
3
Consider the implications
The second possibility emphasizes that causes need not be the familiar ones; God's treasury contains wonders unknown to us.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فقول القائل : يقال له : كن، فيكون غير معقول، إذ التراب لا يخاطب، وانقلابه إنساناً، دون تردده في هذه الأطوار، محال، وتردده في هذه الأطوار، دون جريان هذه الأسباب، محال، فيكون البعث محالا. الاعتراض، أنا نسلم أن الترقى فى هذه الأطوار، لا بد منه، حتى يصير بدن إنسان، كما لا بد منه حتى يصير الحديد عمامة، فإنه لو بقى حديداً لما كان ثوباً، بل لابد أن يصير قطناً، مغزولا، ثم منسوجاً، ولكن ذلك في لحظة، أو فى مدة، ممكن، ولم يبين لنا أن البعث يكون فى أدنى ما يقدر، إذ يمكن أن يكون جمع العظام، وإنشاز اللحم، وإنباته، في زمان طويل. وليس المناقشة فيه. وإنما النظر فى أن الترقى فى هذه الأطوار، يحصل بمجرد القدرة، من غير واسطة، أو بسبب من الأسباب، وكلاهما ممكنان عندنا، على ما ذكرناه في، من الطبيعيات عند الكلام على إجراء العادات، وأن المقترنات في الوجود، اقترانها ليس على طريق التلازم، بل العادات يجوز خرقها، فتحصل بقدرة الله تعالى هذه الأمور، دون وجود أسبابها. وأما الثانى، فهو أن نقول: ذلك يكون بأسباب، ولكن ليس من شرطه، أن يكون السبب، هو هذا المعهود، بل في خزانة المقدورات، عجائب وغرائب، لم يطلع عليها، ينكرها من يظن، أن لا وجود إلا لما شاهده، كما ينكر طائفة، السحر، والنارنجات، والطلسمات، والمعجزات، والكرامات ثابتة - بالاتفاق - بأسباب غريبة، لا يطلع عليها. بل لو لم ير إنسان المغناطيس، وجذ به للحديد، وحكى له ذلك، لاستنكره، وقال: لا يتصور جذب الحديد، إلا بخيط يشد عليه، ويجذب، فإنه المشاهد فى الجذب؛ حتى إذا شاهده تعجب منه، وعلم أن علمه قاصر، عن الإحاطة بعجائب القدرة. وكذلك الملاحدة المنكرون للبعث والنشور، إذا بعثوا من القبور، ورأوا عجائب صنع الله تعالى فيهم، ندموا ندامة لا تنفعهم، ويتحسرون على جحودهم، تحسراً لا يغنيهم، ويقال لهم: « هذا الذي كنتم به تكذبون » كالذي يكذب بالخواص والأشياء الغريبة. بل لو خلق إنسان عاقلا ابتداء، وقيل له: إن هذه النطفة القذرة، المتشابهة الأجزاء، تنقسم أجزاؤها المتشابهة، في رحم آدمية، إلى أعضاء مختلفة، لحمية، وعصبية، وعظمية، وعرقية، وغضروفية، وشحمية، فيكون منها العين، على سبع طبقات مختلفة فى المزاج؛ واللسان، والأسنان، على تفاوتهما في الرخاوة والصلابة، مع تجاورهما، وهلم جرا، إلى البدائع التي في الفطرة - لكان إنكاره أشد من إنكار الملاحدة، حيث قالوا: « كنا عظاماً نخرة . . . الآية ». فليس يتفكر المنكر للبعث، أنه من أين عرف انحصار أسباب الوجود، شاهده، ولم يبعد أن يكون فى إحياء الأبدان، منهاج غير ما شاهده، وقد ورد فى بعض الأخبار: أنه يغمر الأرض فى وقت البعث، مطر، قطراته تشبه النطف، وتختلط بالتراب، فأى بعد فى أن يكون فى الأسباب الإلهية أمر يشبه ذلك، ونحن لا نطلع عليه، ويقتضى ذلك انبعاث الأجساد، واستعدادها لقبول النفوس المحشورة، وهل لهذا الإنكار مستند، إلا الاستبعاد المجرد.
So he who says: 'Be' and it is, is not intelligible, for dust is not addressed, and its transformation into a human without passing through these stages is impossible, and its passing through these stages without the occurrence of these causes is impossible, so the resurrection is impossible. The objection: we concede that progression through these stages is necessary until it becomes a human body, just as it is necessary until iron becomes a turban, for if it remained iron it would not be a garment, but rather it must become cotton, spun, then woven, but that in a moment or in a duration is possible, and he did not make clear to us that the resurrection occurs in the shortest possible time, for it is possible that the gathering of bones, the raising of flesh, and its growth take a long time. And the discussion is not about that. Rather the consideration is that the progression through these stages occurs by mere power without an intermediary, or by a cause from among the causes, and both are possible according to us, as we mentioned in the natural sciences in the discussion of the continuity of habits, and that the conjunctions in existence are not in the way of necessary concomitance, but rather habits may be broken, so these matters occur by the power of God, the Exalted, without the existence of their causes. As for the second, it is that we say: that occurs by causes, but it is not a condition that the cause be this familiar one, but rather in the treasury of possibilities are wonders and marvels that have not been disclosed, which he denies who thinks that nothing exists except what he has witnessed, just as a group denies magic, charms, talismans, miracles, and the extraordinary feats of saints - firmly established by agreement - by strange causes that are not disclosed. Rather, if a man had never seen the magnet and its attraction of iron, and it was related to him, he would reject it and say: the attraction of iron is not conceivable except by a string tied to it and pulled, for that is what is witnessed in attraction, until he sees it and marvels at it and knows that his knowledge is insufficient to encompass the wonders of power. Likewise the atheists who deny the resurrection and the gathering, when they are resurrected from the graves and see the wonders of God's making in them, they will regret a regret that does not benefit them, and they will be remorseful over their denial with a remorse that does not avail them, and it will be said to them: 'This is what you used to deny' like one who denies the properties and strange things. Rather, if an intelligent human were created from the beginning and it was said to him: this filthy drop of fluid, uniform in its parts, its uniform parts divide in a human womb into different members: fleshy, nervous, bony, venous, cartilaginous, and fatty, and from them come the eye of seven different layers in temperament, and the tongue, and the teeth, different in softness and hardness despite their proximity, and so on to the wonders in nature - his denial would be stronger than the denial of the atheists when they said: 'We were decayed bones... [the verse]'. So the denier of resurrection does not reflect: from where does he know the confinement of the causes of existence to what he has witnessed, and it is not remote that in the reviving of bodies there is a method other than what he has witnessed, and it has come in some reports: that at the time of the resurrection, a rain will flood the earth, its drops resembling sperm, and they mix with the dust, so what impossibility is there that in the divine causes there is something resembling that, and we are not informed of it, and that necessitates the rising of the bodies and their readiness to receive the gathered souls, and does this denial have any basis except mere improbability?
Source pages p. 302

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the argument that bodily resurrection is impossible. Ghazali begins by presenting the opponents' objection: to say 'Be' to dust is unintelligible because dust cannot be addressed, and transformation of dust into a human body without passing through natural stages (like conception, growth, etc.) is impossible, and passing through those stages without their usual causes is also impossible, therefore resurrection is impossible. Ghazali's first response is to concede the necessity of stages but to question the required duration. He argues that the stages could occur either in an instant or over a long period—both are possible. The opponent has not specified that resurrection must occur in the shortest time; it could be gradual. Then Ghazali moves to the core of the issue: whether the progression through stages happens by divine power directly without any cause, or through some cause (not necessarily the familiar ones). Both are possible in his view. He references his discussion in natural philosophy where he argued that the constant conjunction of events is not due to necessary causation but to divine habit, which can be broken. So God can bring about these changes directly without their usual causes. The second possibility is that they occur through causes, but not the specific causes we are familiar with. God's treasury of possibilities contains wonders that those who limit existence to what they have witness deny. Ghazali then illustrates with the example of magnetism: someone who has never seen a magnet attract iron would think it impossible without a string, but upon seeing it, he realizes his ignorance. Similarly, atheists who deny resurrection will regret their denial when they witness it. Ghazali then draws a powerful analogy: if a rational person were created from scratch and told about embryological development—from a uniform drop to distinct organs, the eye with seven layers, the tongue and teeth with different textures—his denial would be even stronger than the atheists' denial of resurrection. So the denier of resurrection should reflect: why does he think that the only possible causes are those he has seen? There could be divine methods unknown to him, such as a rain of sperm-like drops at the resurrection. Thus, denial is based on mere improbability, not impossibility.

Key Terms
القدرة
الأسباب
العادات
المعجزات
الكرامات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Resurrection can only occur through the same natural causes we observe in this world.
Correction: Ghazali argues that God can either act directly without any cause, or use causes that are hidden from us, so the familiar causes are not necessary.

Checkpoint
According to Ghazali, how can the progression of stages occur?
A) Only by God's direct power
B) Only through hidden causes
C) Either directly or through causes, whether familiar or not
D) Only through familiar natural causes

Key Takeaway
Ghazali argues that resurrection can occur either by direct divine power or through hidden causes, both of which are possible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In what area of your life do you implicitly assume that God cannot act without the familiar causes—your job, health, relationships—and do you genuinely trust that He can bring about change from His treasury without any intermediary? Will you pray today for something that seems causally impossible?
?
When you hear about miracles or divine interventions, do you inwardly qualify them as 'exceptions' rather than examples of God's normal power? What would change in your daily reliance on God if you truly believed that His treasury is full of wonders you have never seen?
?
If you limit what is possible to what you have witnessed, are you not denying the very basis of faith—that God's power exceeds all expectations? Will you commit this week to meditate on one verse or hadith that describes God's limitless power and let it reshape your expectations?

Causality and Created Things

Examples of Ignorance and the Impossibility of Denial
Ghazali illustrates the irrationality of denying resurrection through examples of magnetism and embryology.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Ghazali uses examples like magnetism and embryology to show that denial based on unfamiliarity is irrational, and that resurrection denial is based on mere improbability.

Core Idea
Denial of resurrection is like denying the magnet's attraction before seeing it — it reflects ignorance of divine power.

Ghazali supports his argument with vivid examples. He compares the denial of resurrection to someone who rejects magnetism because he hasn't seen it. He also draws an analogy with embryological development: if someone were created anew and told about the development from a drop to a complex human, he would deny it even more strongly. This shows that the atheists' denial is based on limited experience, not on impossibility.

Guided Path
1
Read the magnet example
Read from 'بل لو لم ير إنسان المغناطيس...' to '...علمه قاصر.' Understand how unfamiliarity leads to denial.
2
Read the embryology analogy
Read 'بل لو خلق إنسان عاقلا ابتداء...' to the end of the passage. Notice how even more amazing natural processes are denied when not witnessed.
3
Reflect on the conclusion
Ghazali concludes that denial of resurrection is based on mere improbability, not logical impossibility.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Only what we have observed can exist.

Checkpoint
What does the magnet example illustrate?
A) That iron can only be attracted by a string
B) That people often deny what they have not witnessed
C) That resurrection is impossible
D) That God uses only familiar causes

Key Takeaway
Denial of resurrection is based on limited human experience, not on rational proof; just as many natural wonders are initially denied, so resurrection will be witnessed.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
What is one thing in your life—a dua you've given up on, a situation you think is hopeless, or a truth about Allah's power that you've intellectualized but not felt—that you have effectively denied because you have not seen it happen? Will you repent from this limitation of your belief and actively ask Allah to show you His power in that area today?
?
When you look at the creation of a human being from a drop of fluid—the eye with seven layers, the tongue and teeth side by side yet different—do you truly marvel at Allah's power, or do you take it for granted? How can you cultivate a sense of wonder that would prevent you from denying other works of Allah, including the resurrection?
?
The deniers will regret their denial when they see the truth. If you were to die tonight and stand before Allah, what would you regret not believing in that you should have? What concrete step will you take this week to act on that belief, moving from mere intellectual acceptance to heartfelt conviction?

Causality and Created Things

The Oneness of Divine Action: Objection and Response
Objection and response about the oneness and consistency of divine action.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the philosophical objection that divine action has a single fixed course and the response that the divine will, being one, produces a consistent order regardless of apparent variations.

Core Idea
Divine action has one fixed course because the divine will is one and unchanging.

This passage presents a key objection against the possibility of change in divine action, grounded in Quranic proofs for the unchanging nature of God's ways. The response defends the coherence of divine action by emphasizing the unity of the divine will, which ensures that all that emanates from it follows a uniform pattern. As we read, notice how the argument appeals both to scripture and rational consistency.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection and its scriptural basis
Read the first part of the passage where the objector claims divine action has one fixed course and cites Quranic verses. What is the reasoning behind this claim?
The verses are about God's command being one and His way having no change.
2
Examine the first response: consistency and endless recurrence
The passage then addresses the possibility of change: if such causes were possible, they would need to be consistent and recur endlessly. Why does the objector think this is necessary?
3
Understand the second response: unity of divine will
The final part explains that any change would still follow a single pattern because the divine will is not multiple. How does this resolve the objection?
The divine will's oneness ensures that whatever occurs is ordered uniformly, like causes and effects in the world.
4
Reflect on the overall argument
Consider how the objection and response together defend the coherence of divine action. Why is it important for the objector to claim a single fixed course, and how does the response accommodate apparent variation?
The key is that uniformity does not rule out change, as long as the change follows a consistent pattern.

فإن قيل : الفعل الإلهى له مجرى واحد مضروب ، لا يتغير ، ولذلك قال الله تعالى : [ وما أمرنا إلا واحدة كلمح البصر ] وقال تعالى : [ ولن تجد لسنة الله تبديلا ] ، وهذه الأسباب التي توهمتم إمكانها ، إن كانت ، فينبغي أن تطرد أيضاً ، وتتكرر إلى غير نهاية ، وأن يبقى هذا النظام الموجود في العالم ، من التولد والتوالد ، إلى غير نهاية . وبعد الاعتراف بالتكرر والدور ، فلا يبعد أن يختلف منهاج الأمور ، في كل ألف ألف سنة مثلا ، ولكن يكون ذلك التبدل أيضاً دائماً أبداً ، على سنن واحد ، فإن سنة الله تعالى ، لا تبديل فيها . وهذا إنما كان ، لأن الفعل الإلهى ، يصدر على المشيئة الإلهية ، والمشيئة الإلهية ، ليست متعددة الجهة ، حتى يختلف نظامها باختلاف جهاتها ، فيكون الصادر منها كيفما كان منتظماً انتظاماً يجمع الأول والآخر على نسق واحد ، كما تراه في سائر الأسباب والمسببات.
If it is said: The divine action has one fixed course, it does not change. Therefore God Almighty said: 'And Our command is but one, like the blink of an eye' (Quran 54:50) and said: 'And you will never find a change in the way of Allah' (Quran 35:43). And these causes whose possibility you imagine, if they were, then they should also be consistent and recur endlessly, and this existing order in the world, of generation and reproduction, should continue endlessly. And after acknowledging recurrence and cycle, it is not far that the course of affairs differs, for example every thousand thousand years, but that change would also be perpetual, on one pattern, for the way of Allah Almighty has no change in it. This is only because the divine act proceeds from the divine will, and the divine will is not multiple in aspect, so that its system would differ with the difference of its aspects. Rather, what emanates from it, however it may be, is arranged with an arrangement that combines the first and the last on one uniform pattern, as you see in all other causes and effects.
Source pages p. 304

Commentary
This passage is an objection and an initial response concerning the nature of divine action. The objector claims that divine action has a single fixed course that never changes, citing Quranic verses. The response explains that the divine will is not multiple in aspect, so whatever emanates from it follows a consistent order. The passage then extends the objection: if any changes were possible, they would have to be repetitive and endless, but even then the overall pattern remains uniform because the will is one. The commentary of the text uses the example of causes and effects to illustrate consistency.

Key Terms
الفعل الإلهي
المشيئة الإلهية
المجرى الواحد
سنة الله

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the oneness of divine action implies absolute uniformity without any multiplicity at all.
Correction: The passage explains that the divine will is one, so its emanations follow a consistent pattern, but this does not preclude variations within that pattern (e.g., different events at different times) as long as they are part of a uniform order.

Checkpoint
According to the objector in this passage, why must divine action have one fixed course?
A) Because God is powerful over everything.
B) Because the divine will is multiple in aspect.
C) Because God's command is one and His way does not change, as stated in the Quran.
D) Because the world is eternal.

Key Takeaway
The oneness of divine action is rooted in the unity of the divine will, which ensures that all that occurs follows a consistent pattern, even if it includes apparent variations.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face unexpected hardship, do you believe that it too is part of the single, uniform pattern of divine will, or do you feel that God's plan is inconsistent? What would change if you truly internalized that the divine will is one and unchanging?
?
Think of a recurring struggle in your life that seems to repeat. Can you see how it fits into a larger, consistent pattern that God has ordained? How can acknowledging the oneness of divine will help you respond with patience and trust instead of frustration?
?
The objector thought uniformity means no room for change. But the response says change can occur within a uniform pattern. Is there an area of your life where you resist change because you think it contradicts God's consistency? How can you reconcile the two and embrace change as part of God's one will?

Causality and Created Things
beginner
4 min
The Denial of Resurrection Through Repetition
Ghazali's first argument: repetition of the current order negates the uniqueness of resurrection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why allowing repetition of the observed natural order leads to a denial of the uniqueness of the resurrection.

Core Idea
Repetition of natural cycles would make resurrection a recurring event, contradicting Islamic eschatology.

Imam Ghazali presents a powerful dilemma against those who posit cycles. The first horn shows that if the current order of reproduction and procreation continues indefinitely or returns, then resurrection would be a repeated event—directly contradicting the clear teachings of the Law about a unique Day of Judgment. Let's examine this argument.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first conditional scenario
Read the passage and locate where Ghazali sets up the condition of allowing repetition of the current order. Notice the language: 'If you allow the continuation of reproduction and procreation...'
This scenario is the basis for the dilemma.
2
Understand the implication of multiple resurrections
Ghazali argues that if repetition is allowed, then resurrection must have occurred multiple times before our existence and will occur again repeatedly. Trace this reasoning in the text.
The text says: 'then it would be necessary that before this existence of ours, resurrection has occurred multiple times, and will occur multiple times.'
3
Reflect on the contradiction with Islam
Consider why this contradicts Islamic teachings: the Hereafter is a single, final event. The passage states that this view 'denies the resurrection and the Hereafter, and what the apparent meanings of the Law have indicated.'
Islam affirms a single resurrection for judgment, not repeated cycles.
4
Connect to the broader argument
This is the first horn of a dilemma. The second horn (total change) is also impossible. Note how Ghazali uses this to refute the philosophers' position.
The passage continues with the second horn in the same text.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن جوزتم استمرار التوالد والتناسل ، بالطريق المشاهد الآن ، أو عود المنهاج ، ولو بعد زمان طويل ، على سبيل التكرار والدوام ، فقد رفعتم القيامة والآخرة ، وما دل عليه ظواهر الشرع ، إذ يلزم عليه أن يكون ، قد تقدم على وجودنا هذا ، البعث ، كرات ، وسيعود كرات ، وهكذا على الترتيب وإن قلتم إن السنة الإلهية بالكلية ، تتبدل إلى جنس آخر ، ولا تعود قط هذه السنة ، وتنقسم مدة هذا الإمكان ، إلى ثلاثة أقسام : قسم قبل خلق العالم ، إذ كان الله تعالى ولا عالم . بعد خلقه على هذا الوجه وقسم وقسم به الاختتام ، وهو المنهاج البعثى بطل الاتساق والانتظام ، وحصل التبديل لسنة الله تعالى ، وهو محال ، فإن هذا إنما يمكن بمشيئة مختلفة ، باختلاف الأحوال ، أما المشيئة الأزلية ، فلها مجرى واحد مضروب ، لا تتبدل عنه ، لأن الفعل مضاه للمشيئة ، والمشيئة على سنن واحد لا تختلف بالإضافة إلى الأزمان .
For if you allow the continuation of reproduction and procreation in the way now observed, or the return of the course, even after a long time, on the basis of repetition and perpetuity, then you have denied the resurrection and the Hereafter, and what the apparent meanings of the Law have indicated. For it would then be necessary that before this existence of ours, resurrection has occurred multiple times, and will occur multiple times, and so on in order. And if you say that the divine way entirely changes to another kind, and that this way never returns, and the duration of this possibility is divided into three sections: a section before the creation of the world, when God existed and no world existed; a section after creating it in this manner; and a section with which it concludes, which is the eschatological course – then coherence and order are nullified, and change occurs in the way of God Almighty, which is impossible. For this is only possible with a will that differs according to different states. As for the eternal will, it has one fixed course from which it does not change, because the act is parallel to the will, and the will is on one pattern and does not differ with respect to times.
Source pages p. 304

Commentary
This passage is a double-edged refutation of the philosophers' position. First, it shows that if they accept the possibility of repeated cycles of generation and reproduction, then resurrection would have already occurred many times before our existence and will occur again, which contradicts Islamic teachings about the uniqueness of the Hereafter. Second, if they claim that the divine way entirely changes into a different kind (i.e., a completely new order), then the entire system would lose coherence and change would occur in God's way, which is impossible because the eternal will is single and unchanging. The argument underscores that the eternal will does not vary with times, so any fundamental change is ruled out.

Key Terms
القيامة والآخرة
التوالد والتناسل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That allowing natural cycles to continue indefinitely is harmless and does not affect theological beliefs.
Correction: Ghazali shows that this leads to a denial of the unique, final resurrection as taught in Islam.

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is a consequence of allowing the repetition of the current order (التوالد والتناسل) indefinitely?
A) The world would become eternal.
B) The resurrection would have occurred multiple times, denying the uniqueness of the Hereafter.
C) The divine will would become multiple.
D) The divine way would become completely different.

Key Takeaway
Allowing repetition of the natural order leads logically to multiple resurrections, which contradicts Islamic belief in a single Day of Judgment.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you truly believed that this life is the only chance before a single, irreversible meeting with Allah, how would you prioritize your time today? What would you do differently right now?
?
Do you live as if the patterns of this world will continue forever, or do you act with the urgency of someone expecting the final resurrection at any moment? What habit or thought betrays your true belief?
?
Your will changes daily with your moods, but Allah's will is fixed and unchanging. In what area of your life are you resisting alignment with His eternal will? What step will you take today to surrender that area to Him?
