The Impossibility of Total Change in the Divine Way
Ghazali's second argument: total change in the divine way is impossible due to the unchanging eternal will.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why claiming that the divine way entirely changes is impossible, given the unchanging nature of the eternal will.

Core Idea
Total change in God's way is impossible because the eternal will is single, fixed, and unchanging.

After refuting the possibility of repetition, Ghazali turns to the second horn: the claim that the divine way entirely changes to a different kind. He argues that this would disrupt the coherence of God's creation and imply a change in the eternal will—something impossible. Let's explore this argument.

Guided Path
1
Identify the second conditional scenario
Read the passage from 'And if you say that the divine way entirely changes...' and understand the claim being refuted.
This is the alternative to repetition: that the current order is completely replaced by a new one.
2
Understand the three divisions of possibility
Ghazali mentions that the duration of possibility is divided into three sections: before creation, after creation (current order), and the eschatological section. Note how this structure is meant to show that the entire system would lose coherence if change occurs.
The text says: 'coherence and order are nullified, and change occurs in the way of God Almighty, which is impossible.'
3
Analyze the argument against change in the eternal will
Ghazali argues that such total change would require a will that differs according to different states. But the eternal will has one fixed course and does not change with times.
The act is parallel to the will; if the will is unchanging, the act must reflect that constancy.
4
Reflect on the theological implication
This argument reinforces the immutability of God's attributes, particularly His will, and shows that any fundamental change in the order of creation would contradict that immutability.
Hence, neither repetition nor total change is acceptable.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن جوزتم استمرار التوالد والتناسل ، بالطريق المشاهد الآن ، أو عود المنهاج ، ولو بعد زمان طويل ، على سبيل التكرار والدوام ، فقد رفعتم القيامة والآخرة ، وما دل عليه ظواهر الشرع ، إذ يلزم عليه أن يكون ، قد تقدم على وجودنا هذا ، البعث ، كرات ، وسيعود كرات ، وهكذا على الترتيب وإن قلتم إن السنة الإلهية بالكلية ، تتبدل إلى جنس آخر ، ولا تعود قط هذه السنة ، وتنقسم مدة هذا الإمكان ، إلى ثلاثة أقسام : قسم قبل خلق العالم ، إذ كان الله تعالى ولا عالم . بعد خلقه على هذا الوجه وقسم وقسم به الاختتام ، وهو المنهاج البعثى بطل الاتساق والانتظام ، وحصل التبديل لسنة الله تعالى ، وهو محال ، فإن هذا إنما يمكن بمشيئة مختلفة ، باختلاف الأحوال ، أما المشيئة الأزلية ، فلها مجرى واحد مضروب ، لا تتبدل عنه ، لأن الفعل مضاه للمشيئة ، والمشيئة على سنن واحد لا تختلف بالإضافة إلى الأزمان .
For if you allow the continuation of reproduction and procreation in the way now observed, or the return of the course, even after a long time, on the basis of repetition and perpetuity, then you have denied the resurrection and the Hereafter, and what the apparent meanings of the Law have indicated. For it would then be necessary that before this existence of ours, resurrection has occurred multiple times, and will occur multiple times, and so on in order. And if you say that the divine way entirely changes to another kind, and that this way never returns, and the duration of this possibility is divided into three sections: a section before the creation of the world, when God existed and no world existed; a section after creating it in this manner; and a section with which it concludes, which is the eschatological course – then coherence and order are nullified, and change occurs in the way of God Almighty, which is impossible. For this is only possible with a will that differs according to different states. As for the eternal will, it has one fixed course from which it does not change, because the act is parallel to the will, and the will is on one pattern and does not differ with respect to times.
Source pages p. 304

Commentary
This passage is a double-edged refutation of the philosophers' position. First, it shows that if they accept the possibility of repeated cycles of generation and reproduction, then resurrection would have already occurred many times before our existence and will occur again, which contradicts Islamic teachings about the uniqueness of the Hereafter. Second, if they claim that the divine way entirely changes into a different kind (i.e., a completely new order), then the entire system would lose coherence and change would occur in God's way, which is impossible because the eternal will is single and unchanging. The argument underscores that the eternal will does not vary with times, so any fundamental change is ruled out.

Key Terms
السنة الإلهية
المشيئة الأزلية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That God's way (the natural order) can fundamentally change to a completely new order without affecting His attributes.
Correction: Ghazali argues that any change in God's way implies a change in the eternal will, which is impossible because the will is single and unchanging.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is total change in the divine way impossible?
A) Because the world is eternal and cannot change.
B) Because the eternal will has a single, fixed course and does not change.
C) Because the Law forbids any change.
D) Because resurrection would then occur multiple times.

Key Takeaway
The unchanging nature of the eternal will precludes any fundamental change in the divine way, refuting the philosophers' claim of a completely new order.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that the divine order of resurrection and judgment is as fixed and certain as the sun rising tomorrow, or do you live as if there is a chance it might not happen? How does Ghazali's argument about the unchanging eternal will expose any hidden doubts you have about the Hereafter? Write down one concrete step you will take today to realign your life with the certainty of that fixed course.
?
When you consider your past sins, do you assume that God's way might somehow make an exception for you—that the eternal will can bend to accommodate your comfort? Ghazali says the will has 'one fixed course from which it does not change.' What does that demand from you right now regarding a specific sin you have been excusing? Name it, and decide one action to break its hold on you before midnight.
?
This lesson divides time into three sections: before creation, the current order, and the eschatological conclusion. In which of these sections are you investing your heart most? If the current order is the only time for action, and it will not change, what urgent responsibility have you been avoiding that you must face today—not tomorrow?
